\lexicalunitbracket{rihwaˀehsd} \trs{blame someone}

{\punctual} \cayuga{ahsríhwa̱ˀehs} \trs{you are blaming something}

\lexicalunitbracket{rihwaˀehsdę, rihwaˀehsdanih} \trs{demand an audience from someone}

{\punctual} \cayuga{ęhǫwadi:hwáˀehsdęˀ} \trs{they will unravel his message, demand an audience from him}

\lexicalunitbracket{rihwahniyaˀd} \trs{marry someone}

{\stative} \cayuga{shagodi:hwahníya̱ˀdǫh} \trs{they got married by the Chiefs}, \trs{a marriage ceremony} (usually sanctioned by the Chiefs), (literally, \trs{they hardened them})

\lexicalunitbracket{rihwanǫhǫkw} \trs{care for, respect someone’s ideas}

{\punctual} \cayuga{a:goihwanǫ́hkwa:k} \trs{I should care for, respect your ideas}

\lexicalunitbracket{rihwawaˀs} \trs{support someone, agree with someone, back up someone}

{\punctual} \cayuga{ęhehsrihwá:waˀs} \trs{you will back up his ideas}

\lexicalunitbracket{rihwęhdę} \trs{give someone an important message}

{\punctual} \cayuga{ęgǫihwę́hdęˀ} \trs{I will give you a significant message}

\lexicalunitbracket{rǫhyagęˀd} \trs{make someone work hard or labour}, \trs{make someone groan with effort}

{\punctual} \cayuga{ęhsaǫhyágę̱ˀdahk} \trs{it is going to make you groan}

\lexicalunitbracket{ˀshęnyǫgw, ˀshęny} \trs{overpower someone} (physically)

{\habitual} \cayuga{sheˀshę́:nyǫhs} \trs{you are always overpowering someone}, \trs{you are overpowering someone right now}

{\punctual} \cayuga{ęhsheˀshę́:niˀ} \trs{you will overpower someone}

{\stative} \cayuga{sheˀshę́nyǫgwęh} \trs{you have overpowered someone} (a long time ago)

\end{multicols}

{\punctual} \cayuga{ahǫwadiya̱ˀdáhe:ˀ} \trs{they gave him an operation}

\lexicalunitbracket{yahsd} \trs{name someone, something}

{\stative} \cayuga{hodíya̱hsdǫh} \trs{they have named it}

{\punctual} \cayuga{ęhsyé:saht} \trs{you will condemn, slander, insult someone}

\end{multicols}



\section{List of e-verbs} \label{List of verbs of motion}
The (\textsc{e-verb}) or simple verb of motion  \stem{e} \trs{go} only takes \textsc{a}-series prefixes. In contrast, complex motion verbs with \stem{e} \trs{go} take either \textsc{a}, \textsc{p}, or \textsc{interactive} pronominal prefixes. See (\sectref{ch:Simple and complex motion verb prefix choice}.) Examples are provided in the following sections. 

\subsection{Simple verb of motion \stem{e} \trs{go} with \textsc{a}-series personal prefixes} \label{Simple verbs of motion with A personal pronominal prefixes}

\begin{multicols}{2}

\lexicalunitbracket{e} \trs{go, move, be someplace}

\cayuga{iheˀs} \trs{he is here}

\cayuga{ęhsne:ˀ} \trs{you two will go together}

\cayuga{í:geˀ} \trs{I am walking, moving}


\lexicalunitbracket{e} \trs{come here or this way, be here}, with \stem{{\cislocative}}

\cayuga{dagę́:neˀ} \trs{they (z) are coming} 


\lexicalunitbracket{e} \trs{wander}, \trs{be on that side}, with \cayuga{ę:} \trs{side} \cayuga{tsǫ:} \trs{just} \stem{{\cislocative}} 

\cayuga{ę tsǫ: itseˀs} \trs{you wander (all the time)}, \trs{you are over there}


\lexicalunitbracket{e} \trs{come this way}, \trs{be (from) here}, with \cayuga{gaǫ} \trs{somewhere} \stem{{\partitive},{\cislocative}} 

gaoˀ nǫdáhse:ˀ come this way!

\lexicalunitbracket{e} \trs{come back}, \trs{return to here from some place}, with \stem{{\partitive},{\dualic},{\cislocative}} 


\cayuga{naˀdę́:tge:ˀ} \trs{I will come back over here, return}


\lexicalunitbracket{e} \trs{go back}, \trs{return home}, \trs{be back}, with \stem{{\repetitive}}

\cayuga{ihsgeˀs} \trs{I have returned home}

\cayuga{ihsgeˀ} \trs{I am going back}, \trs{I am on my way back}, \trs{I am back (from where I came)}


\lexicalunitbracket{e} \trs{go over there}, \trs{be over there}, with \stem{{\translocative}}

\cayuga{haˀge:ˀ} \trs{I went there}

\lexicalunitbracket{e} \trs{go back there}, \trs{return there}, with \stem{{\translocative},{\repetitive}}

\cayuga{hęhsge:ˀ} \trs{I am going back there}

\end{multicols}


\subsection{Complex verbs of motion with \stem{e} \trs{go}, taking \textsc{a}-series pronominal prefixes} \label{Complex verbs of motion with A personal pronominal prefixes}


\begin{multicols}{2}

\lexicalunitbracket{at-hah-in-e} {\semireflexive}-road-lead-go \newline\trs{walk} 

{\stative} \cayuga{gatahí:neˀ} \trs{I am walking}

\lexicalunitbracket{daks-e} run-go \trs{run} 

{\stative} \cayuga{kdakseˀ} \trs{I am running}

\lexicalunitbracket{daks-enǫ-gy-e} run-originate.from-\textsc{\progressive}-go \trs{run about, roam} 

{\habitual}-{\progressive} \cayuga{gadidaksénǫgyeˀ(s)} \trs{they are running about, roaming}

\lexicalunitbracket{e-:ˀah} {\contrastive}…go-{\diminutive} \trs{walk along any old way} 

{\stative} \cayuga{tihé:ˀah} \trs{he is just walking along}

\lexicalunitbracket{ehd} \trs{do on purpose, go on purpose}

{\habitual} \cayuga{gehtaˀ} \trs{I usually go}

\lexicalunitbracket{ę-nah-awęnye} {\dualic}-…{\semireflexive}-scalp-stir \trs{be crazy, go insane} 

{\punctual} \cayuga{dęsęna̱háwęnye:ˀ} \trs{you will go insane}

{\stative} \cayuga{desęna̱háwęnyeˀ} \trs{you are crazy (not right in the mind)}



\lexicalunitbracket{gy-e} fly/float-go \trs{fly, float} 

{\stative} \cayuga{gegye:ˀ} \trs{I came flying}

{\stative} \cayuga{gagyeˀ} \trs{it is flying along}

\lexicalunitbracket{hręd-e} lead-go \trs{lead} 

{\stative} \cayuga{krę́:deˀ} \trs{I lead, go in front}

\lexicalunitbracket{ˀnyęd-e} try-go \trs{come for a purpose} 

{\stative} \cayuga{se̱ˀnyę́:deˀ} \trs{you came for a purpose}

\lexicalunitbracket{od-agy-e} stand-{\progressive}-go \trs{go along doing something} 

{\stative}-{\progressive} \cayuga{gajiˀdodá:gyeˀ} \trs{someone is going along crying}

\lexicalunitbracket{rad-e} climb-go \trs{climb}

{\stative} \cayuga{srá:deˀ} \trs{you are climbing}

\lexicalunitbracket{yaˀt-gahiy-e}body-agile-go  \trs{be quick, agile} 

{\stative} \cayuga{gyaˀtgahí:yeˀ} \trs{I am quick}



\end{multicols}

\subsubsection*{ \stem{ˀdre} \trs{to drag} versus \stem{(i)ˀdre} \trs{to drive}}
The verbs \stem{ˀdre} \trs{to drag} and \stem{(i)ˀdre} \trs{drive} are similar but take different pronominal prefixes and aspect suffixes. The verb \stem{ˀdre} \trs{to drag} is inflected as a regular three-aspect verb. It takes \textsc{a}-series prefixes with habitual and punctual forms, and \textsc{p} prefixes with stative forms \xref{ex:dragex}.


\ea\label{ex:dragex} \stem{ˀdre} \trs{to drag} 
\ea habitual
\ea ge̱ˀdreˀs \\
\gll ge̱-ˀdre-ˀs\\
\textsc{1s.a}-drag-{\habitual}\\
\glt ‛I drag it'
\ex ge̱ˀdreˀ \\
\gll ge̱-ˀdre-ˀ\\
\textsc{1s.a}-drag-{\habitual}\\
\glt ‛I am dragging it' 
\z
\ex punctual
\ea ęgéˀdre:ˀ\\
\gll ę-gé-ˀdre:-ˀ \\
 \textsc{{\future}-1s.a}-drag-{\punctual}\\
\glt ‛I will drag it'
\ex agéˀdre:ˀ\\
\gll a-gé-ˀdre:-ˀ \\
\textsc{{\factual}-1s.a}-drag-{\punctual}\\
\glt ‛I dragged it' 
\z
\ex stative
\ea agéˀdrǫ: \\
\gll agé-ˀdr-ǫ: \\
\textsc{1s.p}-drag-{\stative}\\
\glt ‛I dragged it, I am dragging it'
\z
\z
\z

In contrast, the motion verb \stem{(i)ˀdre} \trs{to drive, ride along, come by vehicle} takes \textsc{p} prefixes with all aspect forms \xref{ex:drivex}.

\ea\label{ex:drivex} \stem{(i)ˀdre} \trs{drive}, \trs{ride along}, \trs{come by vehicle}
\ea \textsc{habitual}\\
sa̱ˀdreh \\
\gll sa̱-ˀdre-h \\
\textsc{2s.p}-drive-{\habitual}\\
\glt ‛you are driving'
\ex \textsc{punctual}
\ea dędíhsa̱ˀdre:ˀ\\
\gll dędí-hsa̱-ˀdre:-ˀ \\
\textsc{{\dualic}.{\future}.{\cislocative}-2s.p}-drive-{\punctual}\\
\glt ‛you will drive over here'
\ex ędyagodíˀdre:ˀ \\
\gll ę-d-yagodí-ˀdre:-ˀ\\
\textsc{{\future}-{{\cislocative}}-3ns.fi.p}-drive-{\punctual}\\
\glt ‛they will come by vehicle'
\z
\ex \textsc{short \stem{e-ˀ}}\\
agéˀdreˀ\\
\gll agé-ˀdre-ˀ\\
\textsc{1s.p}-ride.along-{\stative}\\
\glt ‛I am riding along'

\ex \textsc{no-aspect}\\
desáˀdre:\\
\gll de-sá-ˀdre:\\
\textsc{{\dualic}-2s.p}-drive.{\noaspect}\\
\glt ‛drive over here'

\z
\z

\subsection{Complex verbs of motion with \stem{e} \trs{go}, taking \textsc{a}-series neuter pronominal prefixes} \label{Complex verbs of motion with A neuter pronominal prefixes}


\begin{multicols}{2}


\lexicalunitbracket{adag-ye-ˀs-ǫˀ} \trs{continue on}, with \stem{{\translocative}-…{\reflexive}-do-{\plural}-{\distributive}} 

{\stative} \cayuga{haˀgadagyéˀsǫˀ} \trs{it continues on endlessly}

\lexicalunitbracket{ag-yenǫ-gy-e} \trs{fly about, float about} \stem{{\semireflexive}-originate.from-float/fly-go}

\lexicalunitbracket{at-hnaw-ine} \trs{flowing liquid} \stem{{\semireflexive}-flowing.water-lead}   

{\stative} \cayuga{watnawí:neˀ} \trs{flowing liquid}

\lexicalunitbracket{hsgo-gy-e} \trs{float (something alive)} \stem{{\noun}-float-go}

\lexicalunitbracket{igyohg-ǫgy-e} \trs{a crowd roaming about} \stem{crowd-{\progressive}-go}

\end{multicols}

\newpage
\subsection{Complex verbs of motion with \stem{e} \trs{go}, taking \textsc{p}-series neuter pronominal prefixes} \label{Complex verbs of motion with O neuter pronominal prefixes}

\begin{multicols}{2}


\lexicalunitbracket{ad-ręd-agy-e} \trs{soar} \stem{{\semireflexive}-hover-{\progressive}-go} 

{\habitual}-{\progressive} \cayuga{odrę́dagyeˀs} \trs{it is soaring (e.g. a bird)}

\lexicalunitbracket{ahjiˀgr-e} \trs{be cloudy} \stem{[cloud-go}

{\stative} \cayuga{ohjíˀgreˀ} \trs{it is cloudy}

\lexicalunitbracket{gy-e} \trs{fly, float} \stem{fly/float-go}

{\stative} \cayuga{ogyeˀ} \trs{it is floating along (in the water)}

\end{multicols}

\subsection{Complex verbs of motion with \stem{e} \trs{go}, taking interactive pronominal prefixes} \label{Complex verbs of motion with gǫ interactive prefixes}

\begin{multicols}{2}


\lexicalunitbracket{hnǫdr-e, hnǫdrę} \trs{follow someone} \stem{follow-go}

{\punctual} \cayuga{ęhéhsnǫdręˀ} \trs{you will follow him}

{\stative} \cayuga{hǫwáhnǫdreˀ} \trs{someone is following him}

\lexicalunitbracket{hnǫdr-agy-e} \trs{follow along with someone} \stem{follow-{\progressive}-go}

{\stative}-{\progressive} \cayuga{hǫwahnǫdrá:gyeˀ} \trs{someone is following him along}

\lexicalunitbracket{hsr-e} \trs{follow someone, chase someone} \stem{follow/chase-go}

{\habitual} \cayuga{hǫwádi̱hsreˀs} \trs{they follow him around all the time}

{\punctual} \cayuga{ęséhsre:ˀ} \trs{you will chase}

{\stative} \cayuga{hadíhsreˀ} \trs{they follow}

\lexicalunitbracket{nęts-in-e} \trs{take someone by the arm} \stem{{\dualic}-arm-lead-go}

{\punctual} \cayuga{ętgǫnętsí:neˀ} \trs{I will take you by the arm}

\end{multicols}

\section{List of counting verbs} \label{List of counting verbs}
Verbs used in counting are listed next. (Counting verbs were previously described in \sectref{ch:Counting with basic nouns}.)


\subsection{\stem{ǫ:} \trs{be a certain amount}, \trs{three or more}, \trs{a few}} \label{[-ǫ:] be a certain amount, three or more, a few}
\ea\label{ex:countingdict1} 
\ea ní:yǫ: \\
\gll ní:-y-ǫ:\\
\textsc{{\partitive}-3s.p}-a.certain.number.{\stative}\\
\glt a certain amount
\newpage
\ex niyǫ́:hah \\
\gll ni-y-ǫ́:-hah\\
\textsc{{\partitive}-3s.p}-a.certain.number.{\stative}-{\diminutive}\\
\glt few, a little bit
\ex haˀdé:yǫ:\\
\gll haˀ-dé:-y-ǫ:\\
\textsc{{\translocative}-{\dualic}-3s.p}-a.certain.number.{\stative}\\
\glt many different things
\ex nigę́:nǫ: \\
\gll ni-gę́:n-ǫ: \\
\textsc{{\partitive}-3p.a}-a.certain.number.{\stative}-{\diminutive}\\
\glt a number of animals
\ex nigá:gǫ: \\
\gll ni-gá:g-ǫ: \\
\textsc{{\partitive}-3ns.fi.a}-a.certain.number.{\stative}-{\diminutive}\\
\glt a number of women, or a mixed group of males and females
\ex ni̱hę́:nǫ:\\
\gll ni̱-hę́:n-ǫ:\\
\textsc{{\partitive}-3ns.m.a.}-a.certain.number.{\stative}-{\diminutive}\\
\glt a number of men
\z
\z


\ea\label{ex:countingdict2} 
\gll dó: ní:yǫ: \\
how a.certain.amount\\
\cayuga{\glt} \trs{how many}, \trs{how much}
\z

\ea\label{ex:countingdict3} 
\gll ne-tóh ní:yǫ: \\
the-that.one a.certain.amount\\
\cayuga{\glt} \trs{that many}, \trs{that much}
\z

\ea\label{ex:countingdict4} 
\gll To: gi̱ˀ–tsǫ́: ní:yǫ:.\\
that.one just–only a.certain.amount\\
\cayuga{\glt} \trs{that’s just all there is}
\z

\ea\label{ex:countingdict5} 
\gll Ęhę́:ˀ do:–gwáˀ ní:yǫ:.\\
yes how–just.so a.certain.amount\\
\cayuga{\glt} \trs{Yes, there are some.}
\z


\ea\label{ex:countingdict6} 
\gll ahsę́h nigę:nǫ́: dagus \\
three a.number.of.animals cats\\
\cayuga{\glt} \trs{three cats}
\z


\ea\label{ex:countingdict7} 
\gll ahsę́h niga:gǫ́: ga:gǫgwéˀdase:\\
three a.number.of.women young.women \\
\cayuga{\glt} \trs{three young women}
\z


\ea\label{ex:countingdict8} 
\gll ahsę́h ni̱hę:nǫ́: hadiksa̱ˀsǫ́:ˀǫh \\
three a.number.of.men boys\\
\cayuga{\glt} \trs{three boys} (\cite{michelson_ontario_2011})
\z

\subsection{\stem{+age:} \trs{a number of items}} \label{[+age:] be a number of things (more than two), [de-…+agehagyeˀ] two at a time}


\ea\label{ex:countingdict9} \stem{{\dualic}-…{\noun}+age:} \trs{two items}
\ea degaˀahdrá:ge: \\
\gll de-ga-ˀahdr-á:ge:\\ 
\textsc{{\dualic}-3s.a}-basket-two.or.more.{\stative}\\
\glt two baskets 
\ex deyohǫnáˀdage: \\
\gll de-yo-hǫnáˀd-age:\\
\textsc{{\dualic}-3s.p}-potato-two.or.more.{\stative}\\
\glt two potatoes
\z
\z

\ea\label{ex:countingdict10} \stem{{\partitive}-…{\noun}+age:} \trs{a number of items}\\
nigana̱ˀjá:ge:\\
\gll ni-ga-na̱ˀj-á:ge:\\
\textsc{{\partitive}-3s.a}-pail-two.or.more.{\stative}\\
\glt ‛an amount of pails, a number of pails' 
\z

\ea\label{ex:countingdict11} \stem{\textsc{number} {\partitive}-…{\noun}+age:}  \trs{three or more items}\\
ahsę́h niyohǫnáˀdage:, ahsę́h nigahǫnáˀdage:\\
\gll ni-yo/ga-hǫnáˀd-age:\\
\textsc{{\partitive}-3s.p/3s.a}-potato-two.or.more.{\stative}\\
\glt ‛three potatoes'
\z

\newpage

\ea\label{ex:countingdict12} \stem{{\dualic}-…{\noun}+agehagyeˀ} \trs{two at a time}\\
degaˀdre̱hdage̱há:gyeˀ \\
\gll de-ga-ˀdre̱hd-age̱-h-á:-gy-e-ˀ\\
\textsc{{\dualic}-3s.a}-car-two.or.more.\textsc{{\stative}-euphonic.h-{\progressive}}-go-{\stative}\\
\glt ‛two cars at at time'
\z



\subsection{\stem{d} \trs{stand} and \stem{ǫd} \trs{attached}} \label{[-d] standing and [-ǫd] be attached}
The verb \stem{d} \trs{stand} is used when counting one object. (See \sectref{[s/j/ji-pronominal prefix-incorporated noun-t]} for more details.)

\ea\label{ex:countingdict13} \stem{{\repetitive}-…{\noun}-{\joinerA}-t} \trs{be one object}\\
sganǫ́hsa:t \\
\gll s-ga-nǫ́hs-a:-t \\
\textsc{{\repetitive}-3s.a}-house-{\joinerA}-stand.{\stative}\\
\glt ‛one house'
\cfex{ganǫ́hsaˀ\\
\gll ga-nǫ́hs-aˀ\\
\textsc{3s.a}-house-\textsc{\nsf}\\
\glt ‛house'}
\z


The verb \stem{ǫd} \trs{attached} can be used to mean \trs{a certain number of attached objects}.

\ea\label{ex:countingdict14} \stem{\textsc{number} {\partitive}-…{\noun}-ǫd} \trs{three or more attached items}\\
ahsę́h niwęˀni̱hsgáǫt\\
\gll ahsę́h ni-w-ęˀni̱hsg-á-ǫt\\
three \textsc{{\partitive}-3s.a}-wheel-{\joinerA}-attached.{\stative}\\
\glt ‛it has three wheels'
\cfex{hyeíˀ niwęˀni̱hsgáǫt\\
\glt ‛it has six wheels'}
\z


\subsection{\stem{\textsc{a}…-yahshe:} \trs{two living things}} \label{[A…-yahshe:] two living things}
\ea\label{ex:countingdict15}
\ea degadiyáhshe: \\
\gll de-gadi-yáhshe: \\
\textsc{{\dualic}-3p.a}-two.living.things.{\stative}\\
\glt {‛two living things'} 
\cfex{degadiyahshé: dagus\\
\glt ‛two cats'}

\newpage
\ex degaeyáhshe: \\
\gll de-gae-yáhshe:\\
\textsc{{\dualic}-3ns.fi.a}-two.living.things.{\stative}\\
\glt ‛two females' (or a male and a female) 
\cfex{degaeyahshé: ga:gǫgwéˀdase:\\
\glt ‛two young women'}
\ex de̱hadiyáhshe:\\
\gll de̱-hadi-yahshe:\\
\textsc{{\dualic}-3ns.m.a}-two.living.things.{\stative}\\
\glt ‛two males'
\cfex{de̱hadiyahshé: hadiksá:ˀah \\
\glt ‛two boys' (\cite{michelson_ontario_2011}}
\z
\z

\subsection{\stem{\textsc{p}…-gaˀdeˀ}  \trs{many}} \label{[O…-gaˀdeˀ] many}

\ea\label{ex:countingdict16}
\ea otgáˀdeˀ\\
\gll o-t-gáˀdeˀ \\
\textsc{3s.p}-{\semireflexive}-many.{\stative}\\
\glt ‛often, many, lots'
\ex odeˀdre̱hdága̱ˀdeˀ\\
\gll o-d-e-ˀdre̱hd-á-ga̱ˀdeˀ\\
\textsc{3s.p-{\semireflexive}}-{\joinerE}-car-many.{\stative}\\
\glt ‛a lot of cars'
\cfex{ga̱ˀdréhdaˀ\\
\gll ga̱-ˀdréhd-aˀ\\
\textsc{3s.a}-car-\textsc{\nsf}\\
\glt ‛car'}

\ex onátga̱ˀdeˀ \\
\gll on-át-ga̱ˀdeˀ \\
\textsc{3p.p}-{\semireflexive}-many.{\stative}\\
\glt ‛lots of, many'
\cfex{onatga̱ˀdéˀ daksáeˀdohs\\
\glt ‛many chickens'}

\ex de̱ˀode̱ˀdrehdagáˀdeˀ\\
\gll de̱ˀ-o-d-e̱-ˀdrehd-a-gáˀdeˀ \\
\textsc{{\negative}-3s.p-{\semireflexive}}-{\joinerE}-car-{\joinerA}-many.{\stative}\\
\glt ‛not many cars'

\newpage
\ex Tréhs gotgáˀdeˀ. Ji̱ˀtréhs gotgáˀdeˀ.\\
\gll (ji̱ˀ)-trehs go-t-gáˀdeˀ \\
too.many \textsc{3ns.fi.p}-{\semireflexive}-many.{\stative}\\
\glt ‛There are too many people'
\ex agéga̱ˀdeˀ \\
\gll agé-ga̱ˀdeˀ \\
\textsc{1s.p}-many.{\stative}\\
\glt ‛I have many' 
\ex aknyǫhsagáˀdeˀ \\
\gll ak-hnyǫhs-a-gáˀdeˀ\\
\textsc{1s.p}-squash-{\joinerA}-many.{\stative}\\
\glt ‛I have a lot of squash'
\z
\z
